3<//rate>
< Review>
Descent local coffee house that serves rather basic fare.
Nothing special in terms of food, since they really do not have a proper full kitchen.  They mostly have items such as muffins & bagels.
If you want a full breakfast with lots of attention, some of the hotels down the road are better choices. Service is what you would expect from a coffee shop. There is no view & it is not especially comfy inside. It feels cramped when crowded.  While it can be a challenge to get a decent breakfast or a cup of coffee in Shell Beach, this is a solid choice
for coffee.  The nearest Starbucks is a few exits away on the 101, so if you just want a cup of Joe, this is it.</Review>

<userid>101816752174202209838<//userid>< name>
J Mog< /name>
< Time>
1581353377632< /Time>
<Rating>3<//Rating>< review>
It's very pretty inside. It's so roomy. The place is beautiful, kudos to the design team!
But the menu is confusing. Is it Indian cuisine, Veitnmese, Korean,...? We ordered the Bahn Mi sandwich, while it was delicious, it's not at all an authentic Bahn Mi, by any means! I would say it's a great Pork Belly Sandwic tho! We also ordered the Bombay Chicken dish, because we crave good Indian food. I would say it was good, if it wasn't marketed as Indian food. However, as an Indian dish It was underwhelming. I think it's fair to say this is American food with cultural vibes. The food was good, but it's not authentic or ethnic.

Our server Britta was icing on the cake. She was charming, attendant, accommodating, cheery and so pleasant. She was a doll! She asked how we liked the Bombay and my husband said it lacked the flavor profile and needed something extra. She offered to get him this spice blend, can't remember what she called it, the spice did add some extra flavor. I loved her ability to serve at a level that has been missing in the restaurant business for some time now. Britta should train all wait staff, she's that good.

Because the cultural vibe is confusing and not authentic, I could not give more stars. If I'm craving Indian food or want an authentic Bahn Mi (that search brought me here, I wanted a good Bahn Mi dang it!) I won't come here. But I would come for the pork belly sandwich.<//review>

< Review>
I'm surprised at some of the low ratings here on Google. The walnut prawns, which are mentioned in some of the negative reviews, are quite good in my opinion; even if they are priced a bit high. It's arguably one of the best items on the menu.

Stay away from the bought-in egg rolls.< /Review>

<Rate>4</Rate><text>Nice friendly waitress. Prices are decent. Steamed rice is hit or miss. Sometimes comes out not completely cooked which is s big no no in Chinese cooking. Most food is excellent. Do not get the hot sour soup. It does not resemble what you would typically get at almost any other Chinese restaurant.i have heard complaints about their hot and sour soup many times I was there. Their won ton soup is good though, as is their egg flour  and rice soup. Their oyster sauce beef is excellent if made by the cook that works mon, wed, and Friday, and ask for no to little onions. Otherwise you will get a ton of them with a few slivers of meat. Lunch plates are decently priced. One neighbor is a bar/club of some sort. They didn't bother to completely isolate their music from being heard in the restaurant. So I tend to sit away from the wall at dinner service. If the sound of thumping bass doesn't bother you, these is a mute point then. When it is packed, it's still just the one waitress but she does do an excellent job of providing service to everyone. Just expect to be patient when its busy. This isn't a fast food restaurant so adjust your expectations of expediency accordingly</text>< pics>

< Review>
Chinese food in Antioch is not good. I've been to every place and none of it is worth going to twice unless you're just really desperate. Wongs is my family's favorite Chinese place in the area so I've had it many times.  It's ok. The food is decent, mainly the dishes that are hard to fail at such as walnut shrimp and other deep fried things. The chow mein is too watery for me but it tastes good.

The must haves here: Wongs fried rice

This should be a 3 and a half star rating but since you can't, they don't get the half star bonus. Also, the owner seems to absolute hate life. He sits there on his chair frowning the entire time... It's pretty awkward and sad. I wish I could some how brighten his day but I can't. I debated giving 4 stars just in case he read this and maybe it'll put the slightest smirk on his face but I realized there's no way he'll be on Yelp.... he's in some cave working on his frown game.

<Response>{'time': 1573613085191, 'text': 'This is Mitch Bailey, owner, I would recommend that you also get three bids on this project. Although you found this price extreme, we were quoting Trane equipment with a very high SEER value along with 97% furnaces, including installation, line set, wifi thermostat, permit, her\'s testing, load calculation, air flow balancing, along with a ten years parts and labor warranty. I doubt you will find a comparable price with the same caliber equipment and an install from a company that has been in business going on 44 years now. Sorry we couldn\'t do business, respectfully Mitch Bailey, P.S. Seriously, you give a low rating because you didn\'t like the bid? In addition, we do have less expensive equipment for those that can not afford the best, if you would like a quote on say, Goodman, we would be happy to oblige.\n\nTalked to Steve as you suggested, he will be more courteous in the future, thanks for that input. The RUUD price you last posted is very cheap to say the least. Our Goodman price for that system would be at least a $1000 more, plus we charge out linesets around $900. This must be a local company with less employees and overhead than we have, in addition, I am not sure they are pulling a permit and having it HER\'s tested-we always do.\n\nAs a side note, I teach this trade for contractors and techs at PG&E in Stockton and for Southern California Edison in Tulare. The subject of pricing comes up quite often as many of the students are HVAC contractors themselves. A good rule of thumb to make a profit between 10% and 20%, is to take the price of the equipment and multiply by a factor that is between 2.5 and up to 3.2. This accounts for overhead, permits, third party testing, labor, and other essentials to replacing or installing a system. The factor will vary according to a company\'s overhead and what they pay their people, we pay on the higher side of the pay scale for our industry. Moreover, the higher the price of the equipment, the lower the multiplier. We actually use a sliding scale for service and parts based on the part price. 0x80946099ccce950f:0x453ec97a1e5155c6< /GmapID>
<text>8/29/2017, at approximately 2:30pm, I entered Burger King on Fresno Street and "B" Street by Rite Aid and Food Max.

I went in for the 2 tacos for $1.49. I told the girl over the counter that I couldn't see the menu on the board without my eyeglasses. She said that there were 2 tacos for a dollar. She charged me $2.16 for 2 tacos. I repeated a few times and I felt like she was dodging me. Finally, I dug into my shoulder bag and pulled out my perscription eyeglasses. Went back to the counter and again ordered those 2 tacos but this time I could then CLEARLY see 2 tacos for $1.49.  This young lady tried again to charge me again $2.16 only this time I pointed out the board. She then got the manager to correct the second order while trying to give me a refund on the first order. The manager (who looked very perturbed towards the cashier) was handing me a dollar with a receipt but the cashier grabbed the money out of my hand and gave me the 2 tacos while keeping the dollar and receipt???

Prior to this whole transaction, I was approached by a young man targeting anyone placing an order, asking for 50 cents, after getting my change (from the other suspect), he then asked for a dollar. He then circled (like a hungry shark), as if to extort that dollar a few more times.
